          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container legacy" data-template="desktop" id="article-survivor-cagayan-finale-and-the-winner-is-041628194" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">

            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">

                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-survivor-cagayan-finale-and-the-winner-is-041628194">
                      'Survivor: Cagayan' Finale: And the Winner Is...
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-survivor-cagayan-finale-and-the-winner-is-041628194" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t provider-info">
                          <div class="provider-alias C-n">
                           <span class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b">
                            Yahoo TV
                           </span>
                          </div>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            Kelly Woo
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             May 22, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-survivor-cagayan-finale-and-the-winner-is-041628194" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           <em>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:a8d7fe20-5ab6-3409-b2c0-abef26a350e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://tv.yahoo.com/photos/meet-the-survivor-cagayan-castaways-1390347012-slideshow/" target="_blank">
                             <div>
                              <img align="middle" alt="'Survivor: Cagayan' Finale: And the Winner Is..." class="editorial" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/SPLA66dnIWE0Og0Mldb7RA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/https://s.yimg.com/os/publish-images/tv/2014-05-22/49e58820-e166-11e3-aeaa-5b6ed538b90c_S28_2814_SG_083b.JPG" title="Spencer Bledsoe and Tony Vlachos on a special two-hour season finale of SURVIVOR, Wednesday, May 21 (8:00-10:00 PM, ET/PT) followed by a live reunion show hosted by Jeff Probst (10:00-11:00PM, ET/PT), on the CBS Television Network. Photo: Screen Grab/CBS &copy;2014 CBS Broadcasting Inc. All Rights Reserved." width="800"/>
                              <p class="legend">
                               Spencer Bledsoe and Tony Vlachos on a special two-hour season finale of SURVIVOR, Wednesday, May 21 (8:00-10:00 PM, ET/PT) followed by a live reunion show hosted by Jeff Probst (10:00-11:00PM, ET/PT), on the CBS Television Network. Photo: Screen Grab/CBS 2014 CBS Broadcasting Inc. All Rights Reserved.
                              </p>
                             </div>
                            </a>
                           </em>
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           <em>
                            Survivor
                           </em>
                           Rule: You can win, or you can be a really loyal loser.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          After 28 seasons,
                          <em>
                           Survivor
                          </em>
                          can still surprise.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In what might be a first, this season's winner, 39-year-old police officer Tony Vlachos, won after a passionate plea to the jury  not from himself, but from jury member Spencer Bledsoe.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           [Related:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:a8d7fe20-5ab6-3409-b2c0-abef26a350e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://tv.yahoo.com/blogs/tv-news/-survivor--cagayan--recap--tony-uses-his-bag-of-tricks--but-will-it-get-him-to-the-end-045006000.html" target="_blank">
                            Get Caught Up With Our 'Survivor' Recaps
                           </a>
                           ]
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Tony and Yung "Woo" Hwang, his ally from the former Brawn tribe, faced off against each other in the final tribal council. At first, the jury members seemed to be leaning away from the backstabbing, blindsiding Tony. But Spencer, who was the last to speak, made a well-reasoned case to vote for the cop.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          "Tony played with a ferocity that this game rarely ever sees," Spencer argued. So, after 39 days, Tony was crowned Sole Survivor and the winner of $1 million.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           <span class="yui-media yui-editorial-embed" style="width:630px;height:354px;">
                           </span>
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <iframe data-src="/video/survivor-cagayan-survivor-winner-announced-050946408-cbs.html?format=embed" height="393.75" width="700">
                          </iframe>
                         </div>
                         <strong>
                          <br/>
                         </strong>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Maybe Tony would've won without Spencer's rare intercession, but we doubt it. And Woo must be kicking himself; had he taken third-place finisher Kass McQuillen to the end, he might be counting that cash right now. In fact, during the reunion, the jury indicated that they wouldve voted for him over Kass.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The season started with three tribes  Beauty, Brains, and Brawn  and oddsmakers bet on Woo being the winner. In the end, it was a Brawn who won... just not Woo.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The three-hour finale and reunion began with four players  Tony, Woo, Kass, and Spencer. In the first immunity challenge, Kass pulled out one of the most incredible comebacks in
                          <em>
                           Survivor
                          </em>
                          history.
                         </p>
                         <span>
                          <div class="yom-figure yom-fig-center" id="ymh-player-iframe" style="left: 0px; background: #cccccc; width: 630px; height: 354px;">
                           <iframe data-src="/video/survivor-cagayan-immunity-challenge-vertigo-010946951-cbs.html?format=embed" height="393.75" width="700">
                           </iframe>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <p>
                          And though Spencer tried his hardest to convince Tony to make it a tie vote (so that he and Woo would have to make fire to break the tie), he was voted out in fourth place.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          In the final immunity challenge, a difficult maze course pushed the three players to their limits. Woo managed to pull out the win just a half-second before Kass, which gave him the power to decide who to take to the final two. Loyalty won out over greed, and Woo chose his ally over Kass.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:a8d7fe20-5ab6-3409-b2c0-abef26a350e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://tv.yahoo.com/photos/meet-the-survivor-cagayan-castaways-1390347012-slideshow/" target="_blank">
                           <span class="yui-media yui-editorial-embed" style="width:630px;height:354px;">
                           </span>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <iframe data-src="/video/survivor-cagayan-immunity-challenge-roundabout-011146887-cbs.html?format=embed" height="393.75" width="700">
                          </iframe>
                         </div>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                         </div>
                         <p>
                          It was a huge mistake, though Woo told the jury that he wanted to play an honorable and loyal game. That argument seemed to resonate with some of the jury members  until Spencer's game-changing speech at the last tribal council.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          And despite Tony's betrayals, his fellow players had mostly forgiven him. Trish Hegarty noted at the reunion that she and Tony still speak regularly. But fellow cop Sarah Lacina said they were no longer on speaking terms.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          "If I didn't break my loyalty to people, if I'd told everybody the truth, I'd be sitting in the jury," Tony said during the reunion.
                         </p>
                         <span>
                          <div class="yom-figure yom-fig-center" id="ymh-player-swf" style="left:0px;">
                           <iframe allowfullscreen="true" allowtransparency="true" data-src="https://tv.yahoo.com/video/insider-video-collection/survivor-winner-opens-competition-211413029.html?format=embed&amp;player_autoplay=false" data-yom-embed-source="{media_id_1:d275b9aa-cdaa-361c-b941-d4b6ec755a27}" frameborder="0" height="354" mozallowfullscreen="true" webkitallowfullscreen="true" width="630">
                           </iframe>
                          </div>
                         </span>

root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

onscreen: the spectacle of a deluded rocker being aced by a shrewd pop-ster.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F275a28c12e715a6bbf38cf8e3bf818b2819a0e03.jpg\" alt=\"&apos;Sex&amp;Drugs&amp;Rock&amp;Roll&apos;: Can Denis Leary Become A Rock Star?\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m pretty sure Denis Leary did not intend his new show \u003Ci\u003ESex&amp;Drugs&amp;Rock&amp;Roll\u003C\u002Fi\u003E to be interpreted this way, but, hey, rock &amp; roll makes up its rules as it goes along: This FX series premiering Thursday makes a very good case for the notion that there&#x2019;s no such thing as authenticity in rock music.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENever one to go for subtlety, Leary stars as a musician named Johnny Rock, a 50 year-old cult star who, we&#x2019;re supposed to believe, could have been a big star if only he hadn&#x2019;t feuded with the Keith Richards to his Mick Jagger, his co-writer\u002Flead-guitarist Flash (John Corbett, whose achievement here is extending his wastrel-musician character from\u003Ci\u003E Parenthood\u003C\u002Fi\u003E into complete degeneracy). Johnny, who still struts around with a rooster hairdo lifted from the head of Rod Stewart circa \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=HLBFyS2hlhw\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EGasoline Alley\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, broke up the band and has been grasping at fame for about three decades now, when his new meal ticket suddenly arrives.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThat meal ticket takes the form of his long-lost daughter, who&#x2019;s got the youth, pipes, and Instagrammed body to give anyone&#x2019;s career a boost, and if you think that sounds crude, that is exactly what show-creator Leary wants you to think when you look at and listen to Gigi. She&#x2019;s played by Elizabeth Gillies, a Broadway and Nickelodeon vet who&#x2019;s immediately convincing as a young professional with daddy issues who is not above using Johnny as cynically as he plans to use her. A warm family sitcom \u003Ci\u003ESex&amp;Drugs\u003C\u002Fi\u003E is not.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-embed tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Ciframe width=\"540\" height=\"304\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FAsmxcw4iFME?feature=oembed\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENeither is it a very funny sitcom. In \u003Ci\u003ERescue Me,\u003C\u002Fi\u003E Leary had the benefit of co-creator Peter Tolan and a deep bench of talented co-stars to whom he was willing to cede the spotlight. This time around, Leary surrounds himself with good actors who are very much the actor-equivalent of a back-up band, and he crowds Gillies for the spotlight in every scene they share. This is not wise when the punchlines he gives himself include, &#x201C;I wanna blow Bruce Jenner&#x201D; and &#x201C;I&#x2019;m not writing some auto-tune Katy Perry bulls&#x2013;t.&#x201D; Maybe I&#x2019;d feel more charitable about this had Leary not co-opted the title of a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=2TBSqS4yMrM\"\u003Egreat Ian Dury song\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and failed to make his own, self-written theme song one-thousandth as good.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou&#x2019;re supposed to think Johnny Rock is a jerk who&#x2019;s actually heroic because he&#x2019;s fighting for the rebel spirit of rock, but I&#x2019;ll bet there are a lot of viewers who&#x2019;ll identify more with Gigi, a realist who&#x2019;s fighting for the freedom that comes with being a pop star nowadays. In Gigi&#x2019;s cosmos &#x2014; and mine &#x2014; Katy Perry is as legit as Steven Tyler, or Jon Bon Jovi, or any other rocker the show invokes.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"335\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Ff7ccab73b890d979bdf6a5d89cb1ae18cb9fe6c8.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETV and rock &amp; roll have a history as long as both mediums. Not just Elvis Presley wiggling from the waist-up on \u003Ci\u003EThe Ed Sullivan Show\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, but also Ricky Nelson smuggling future Presley guitarist James Burton onto the otherwise-anodyne \u003Ci\u003EThe Adventures of Ozzie and Harriet\u003C\u002Fi\u003E (1952-&#x2019;66). From \u003Ci\u003EThe Monkees\u003C\u002Fi\u003E to \u003Ci\u003EEmpire\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, television shows that use pop music as a metaphor for freedom, fame, and wealth have always been compromised projects, some better than others.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow that rock is merely one genre among many from which a singer like Gigi plucks a melody or tempo, the bottom-line message of \u003Ci\u003ESex&amp;Drugs&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#x2014; that one kind of music is privileged with a unique truth &#x2014; is undercut by what&#x2019;s actually onscreen: the spectacle of a deluded rocker being aced by a shrewd pop-ster.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESex&amp;Drugs&amp;Rock&amp;Roll \u003Ci\u003Eairs Thursday at 10 p.m. on FX. Woo managed to pull out the win just a half-second before Kass, which gave him the power to decide who to take to the final two.
